						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Presidents of the United States" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="President of the United States (disambiguation)">President of the United States (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">



</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:White_House_Washington.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/White_House_Washington.JPG/330px-White_House_Washington.JPG" decoding="async" width="320" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/White_House_Washington.JPG/500px-White_House_Washington.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/White_House_Washington.JPG/960px-White_House_Washington.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4163" data-file-height="2440" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>, official residence of the president of the United States</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president of the United States</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERossiter196286_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERossiter196286-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indirectly_elected" class="mw-redirect" title="Indirectly elected">indirectly elected</a> to a four-year <a href="/wiki/Term_of_office" title="Term of office">term</a> via the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College" title="United States Electoral College">Electoral College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShugart2004633–636_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShugart2004633–636-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Under the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Constitution">U.S. Constitution</a>, the officeholder leads the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive branch</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal government</a> and is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEpstein2005318_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEpstein2005318-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The first president, <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>, won a unanimous vote of the Electoral College.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatuz2001xxii_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatuz2001xxii-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The incumbent president is <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Second_inauguration_of_Donald_Trump" title="Second inauguration of Donald Trump">assumed office on January 20, 2025</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHajela2024_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHajela2024-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreile2024_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreile2024-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since the office was established in 1789, 45 men have served in 47 presidencies. The discrepancy is due to the nonconsecutive terms of <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a> (counted as the 22nd and 24th president) and Trump (counted as the 45th and 47th president).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAP2024_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAP2024-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchallerWilliams2003192_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchallerWilliams2003192-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The presidency of <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">William Henry Harrison</a>, who died 31 days after taking office in 1841, was the shortest in American history.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcHughMackowiak2014990–995_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcHughMackowiak2014990–995-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> served the longest, over twelve years, before dying early in his fourth term in 1945. He is the only U.S. president to have served more than two terms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkau1974246–275_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkau1974246–275-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since the ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-second Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twenty-second Amendment to the United States Constitution</a> in 1951, no person may be elected president more than twice, and no one who has served more than two years of a term to which someone else was elected may be elected more than once.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeabodyGant1999565_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeabodyGant1999565-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Four presidents died in office of natural causes (William Henry Harrison, <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">Zachary Taylor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Harding" title="Warren G. Harding">Warren G. Harding</a>, and Franklin D. Roosevelt), four were <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_presidential_assassination_attempts_and_plots" title="List of United States presidential assassination attempts and plots">assassinated</a> (<a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield" title="James A. Garfield">James A. Garfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>), and one resigned (<a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, facing <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_process_against_Richard_Nixon" title="Impeachment process against Richard Nixon">impeachment</a> and removal from office).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005627–644_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005627–644-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Tyler" title="John Tyler">John Tyler</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">vice president</a> to assume the presidency during a presidential term, setting the precedent that a vice president who does so becomes the fully functioning president with a new, distinct administration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDinnerstein1962447–451_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDinnerstein1962447–451-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout most of its history, <a href="/wiki/American_politics" class="mw-redirect" title="American politics">American politics</a> has been dominated by <a href="/wiki/Political_parties_in_the_United_States" title="Political parties in the United States">political parties</a>. The Constitution is silent on the issue of political parties, and at the time it came into force in 1789, no organized parties existed. Soon after the <a href="/wiki/1st_United_States_Congress" title="1st United States Congress">1st Congress</a> convened, <a href="/wiki/Political_faction" title="Political faction">political factions</a> began rallying around dominant <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_Washington" title="Presidency of George Washington">Washington administration</a> officials, such as <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010197Nardulli1992179_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010197Nardulli1992179-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Concerned about the capacity of political parties to destroy the fragile unity holding the nation together, Washington remained <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">unaffiliated</a> with any political faction or party throughout his eight-year presidency. He was, and remains, the only U.S. president who never affiliated with a political party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELOC_(2)Jamison2014_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELOC_(2)Jamison2014-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Presidents">Presidents</h2></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1305414688">@media screen and (min-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .sticky-header>thead>tr:first-child,.mw-parser-output <div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notes">Notes</h2></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239543626">.mw-parser-output .reflist{margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}@media screen{.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%}}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Presidents are numbered according to uninterrupted periods served by the same person. For example, George Washington served two consecutive terms and is counted as the first president, instead of the first and second, but Grover Cleveland and Donald Trump are counted twice because their two terms were not consecutive. A vice president who temporarily becomes <a href="/wiki/Acting_President_of_the_United_States" title="Acting President of the United States">acting president</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-fifth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twenty-fifth Amendment</a> to the Constitution is not counted, because the president remains in office during such a period.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Reflects the president's political party at the start of their presidency. Changes during their time in office are noted. Also reflects the vice president's political party unless otherwise noted beside the individual's name.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Political parties had not been anticipated when the Constitution was drafted, nor did they exist at the time of the first presidential election in 1788–89. When they did develop, during Washington's first term, Adams joined the faction that became the <a href="/wiki/Federalist_Party" title="Federalist Party">Federalist Party</a>. The elections of 1792 were the first ones in the United States that were contested on anything resembling a partisan basis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010197,_272Nardulli1992179_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010197,_272Nardulli1992179-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The 1796 presidential election was the first contested American presidential election and the only one in which a president and vice president were elected from opposing political parties. Federalist John Adams was elected president, and Jefferson of the Democratic-Republicans was elected vice president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010274_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010274-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-diedintraterm-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-diedintraterm_30-14"><sup><i><b>o</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Died in office<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeale200422_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeale200422-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-JQAdams-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-JQAdams_34-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Early during John Quincy Adams' term, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic-Republican_Party" title="Democratic-Republican Party">Democratic-Republican Party</a> dissolved; his allies in Congress and at the state level were referred to as "Adams' Men" during the Adams presidency. When <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a> became president in 1829, this group became the "Anti-Jackson" <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(politics)" title="Opposition (politics)">opposition</a>, and organized themselves as the <a href="/wiki/National_Republican_Party" title="National Republican Party">National Republican Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010228Goldman1951159_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010228Goldman1951159-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">John Calhoun, formerly a Democratic-Republican, founded the <a href="/wiki/Nullifier_Party" title="Nullifier Party">Nullifier Party</a> in 1828 to oppose the <a href="/wiki/Tariff_of_Abominations" title="Tariff of Abominations">Tariff of 1828</a> and advance the cause of <a href="/wiki/States%27_rights" title="States&#39; rights">states' rights</a>, but was brought on as Andrew Jackson's running mate in the 1828 presidential election in an effort to broaden the democratic coalition led by Jackson.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010892Houpt201026,_280_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Guide_to_U.S._Elections&#39;&#39;2010892Houpt201026,_280-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-resignedintraterm-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-resignedintraterm_38-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-resignedintraterm_38-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-resignedintraterm_38-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Resigned from office<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeale200422_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeale200422-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">John Tyler succeeded to the presidency upon the death of William Henry Harrison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbott201323_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbott201323-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-JTyler-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-JTyler_45-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">John Tyler was elected vice president on the Whig Party ticket in 1840. His policy priorities as president soon proved to be opposed to most of the Whig agenda, and he was expelled from the party five months after assuming office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECash201834–36_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECash201834–36-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Millard Fillmore succeeded to the presidency upon the death of Zachary Taylor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005639_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005639-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-ALincoln-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ALincoln_55-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">When he ran for reelection in 1864, Republican Abraham Lincoln formed a bipartisan <a href="/wiki/Electoral_alliance" title="Electoral alliance">electoral alliance</a> with <a href="/wiki/War_Democrat" title="War Democrat">War Democrats</a> by selecting Democrat Andrew Johnson as his running mate, and running on the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_Party_(United_States)" title="National Union Party (United States)">National Union Party</a> ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcSeveney1986139_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcSeveney1986139-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-57">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Andrew Johnson succeeded to the presidency upon the death of Abraham Lincoln.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse2000_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse2000-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AJohnson-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AJohnson_58-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">While president, Andrew Johnson tried and failed to build a coalition of loyalists under the National Union banner. Near the end of his presidency, Johnson began reassociating with the Democratic Party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrefousse2000_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrefousse2000-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-64">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Chester A. Arthur succeeded to the presidency upon the death of James A. Garfield.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreenberger2017174–175_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreenberger2017174–175-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Theodore Roosevelt succeeded to the presidency upon the death of William McKinley.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005639–640_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005639–640-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Calvin Coolidge succeeded to the presidency upon the death of Warren G. Harding.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESenate_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESenate-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Harry S. Truman succeeded to the presidency upon the death of Franklin D. Roosevelt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005636_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005636-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lyndon B. Johnson succeeded to the presidency upon the death of John F. Kennedy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005633_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbbott2005633-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-VP25th-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-VP25th_88-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-VP25th_88-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Appointed as vice president under terms of the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-fifth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twenty-fifth Amendment</a>, Section 2<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeale200422_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeale200422-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gerald Ford succeeded to the presidency upon the resignation of Richard Nixon. Even though Ford served out the remainder of Nixon's second term, he was never elected to the presidency or vice presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreene2013_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreene2013-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
